# Investigation: Phantom In-Place Updates for Resources with Sensitive Attributes in Terraform

**Repository:** github.com/sg-evals/terraform--9658f9df (mirror of hashicorp/terraform)
**Task Type:** Deep Causal Chain (investigation only — no code fixes)

## Scenario

A Terraform user reports that `terraform plan` consistently shows resources "will be updated in-place" even though **no configuration changes** have been made. The phantom update appears for any resource that has provider-schema-defined sensitive attributes (e.g., `password`, `secret_key`).

The user is managing a VPN tunnel resource:

```hcl
resource "test_instance" "example" {
  ami      = "ami-12345"
  password = var.db_password  # provider schema marks 'password' as Sensitive: true
}
```

After a successful `terraform apply`, immediately running `terraform plan` shows:

```
  # test_instance.example will be updated in-place
  ~ resource "test_instance" "example" {
        id       = "i-abc123"
        # (1 unchanged attribute hidden)
    }

Plan: 0 to add, 1 to change, 0 to destroy.
```

There are **no actual attribute changes** — the before and after values are identical. The phantom diff occurs specifically for resources where the provider schema declares one or more attributes with `Sensitive: true`.

Additionally, `terraform show -json` on the state file shows that the `sensitive_values` section in the JSON output is **incomplete** — it lists sensitivity marks that came from variable references (e.g., `var.db_password` is a `sensitive` variable) but **omits** sensitivity marks from the provider schema itself (e.g., the `password` attribute is always sensitive regardless of how it's populated).

Running `terraform plan -refresh-only` also shows phantom changes, and `terraform import` followed by `terraform plan` shows even more phantom updates.

## Your Task

Investigate the root cause of why Terraform generates phantom in-place updates for resources with schema-sensitive attributes, and produce a report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`.

Your report MUST cover:

1. **How provider responses flow through the graph evaluator** — when `ReadResource` (refresh) or `PlanResourceChange` (plan) returns a value from the provider, how does `node_resource_abstract_instance.go` process that response? Specifically, examine `readResourceInstanceState()` (refresh path) and `plan()` (plan path) in `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`.

2. **The sensitivity mark gap** — the provider response comes back **without** any sensitivity marks (providers don't mark values; that's Terraform's responsibility). The code re-applies marks from the **prior state** (`priorPaths` from `AttrSensitivePaths`), but these only contain marks from sensitive variable references, NOT from the provider schema's `Sensitive: true` declarations.

3. **How state serialization records incomplete sensitivity** — when the instance object is written to state via `internal/states/instance_object.go`, `sensitive_attributes` in the state file only has paths from sensitive references, missing the schema-defined sensitive paths. Trace through how `AttrSensitivePaths` is populated and how `unmarkValueForStorage` extracts marks before state serialization.

4. **The evaluator's compensating workaround** — `internal/terraform/evaluate.go`'s `GetResource()` method was the ONLY place that applied schema marks (via `markProviderSensitiveAttributes()` or similar). This meant that when a value was read FROM state and decoded for expression evaluation, it would get schema marks added. But the value stored IN state never had those marks. This created an asymmetry.

5. **How the asymmetry produces phantom diffs** — the plan compares refreshed state (which has schema marks from the evaluator) against the planned state (which was built from provider response without schema marks). The mark difference causes the plan to detect a "change" even though the underlying values are identical. The diff is in the sensitivity metadata, not the attribute values themselves.

6. **The JSON output manifestation** — `internal/command/` layer functions that produce `terraform show -json` read `sensitive_attributes` from state, which is incomplete. This produces incorrect `sensitive_values` in JSON plan/state output, where schema-defined sensitive attributes are missing from the sensitivity map.

## Output Requirements

Write your investigation report to `/logs/agent/investigation.md` with these sections:

```
# Investigation Report

## Summary
<1-2 sentence finding>

## Root Cause
<Specific file, function, and mechanism>

## Evidence
<Code references with file paths and line numbers>

## Affected Components
<List of packages/modules impacted>

## Causal Chain
<Ordered list: symptom → intermediate hops → root cause>

## Recommendation
<Fix strategy and diagnostic steps>
```

## Constraints

- Do NOT write any code fixes
- Do NOT modify any source files
- Your job is investigation and analysis only
- The causal chain spans at least 4 packages: `internal/terraform/` (graph evaluation + marks), `internal/states/` (state serialization), `internal/command/` (JSON output), and the provider interaction boundary
- Focus on how `node_resource_abstract_instance.go` handles provider responses, how `marks.go` applies sensitivity, how `instance_object.go` serializes state, and how `evaluate.go` compensates

     1→# Investigation Report: Phantom In-Place Updates for Resources with Sensitive Attributes
     2→
     3→## Summary
     4→
     5→Terraform generates phantom in-place updates for resources with provider-schema-defined sensitive attributes because the refresh/plan cycle creates an asymmetry in sensitivity mark application. The provider schema's `Sensitive: true` attribute declarations are never persisted to state, causing the evaluator's compensating mark-application logic to create inconsistencies that trigger false "Update" actions when no values have actually changed.
     6→
     7→---
     8→
     9→## Root Cause
    10→
    11→The root cause is a **sensitivity mark gap** between three critical stages:
    12→
    13→1. **State Serialization** (`internal/states/instance_object.go`): When state is written to disk, only sensitivity marks from variable references are saved in `AttrSensitivePaths`; schema-defined sensitive attributes are lost.
    14→
    15→2. **State Deserialization** (`internal/states/instance_object_src.go`): When state is read, marks are re-applied from the incomplete `AttrSensitivePaths`, lacking schema marks.
    16→
    17→3. **Evaluation-Time Compensation** (`internal/terraform/evaluate.go`): The `GetResource()` method applies schema marks when reading from state for expression evaluation, but this compensating layer is NOT applied during plan generation in `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`.
    18→
    19→This asymmetry causes the plan phase to compare:
    20→- **Planned state** (from provider, no marks at all)
    21→- **Prior state** (from state file with incomplete marks, only from variables)
    22→
    23→When the marks differ even though values don't, a phantom "Update" action is triggered.
    24→
    25→---
    26→
    27→##

95-assistanttext-
Excellent! I have completed the investigation and created a comprehensive report at `/logs/agent/investigation.md`. 

## Investigation Summary

The report details the root cause of phantom in-place updates for resources with sensitive attributes in Terraform:

**Key Finding:** A **sensitivity mark asymmetry** exists between state persistence and plan generation:

1. **State Serialization Gap** - Schema-defined sensitive attributes (marked `Sensitive: true` in provider schema) are never persisted to the state file because they're only applied during expression evaluation, not during state encoding.

2. **Incomplete Mark Reapplication** - When state is read during planning, only sensitivity marks from variable references are re-applied, missing schema-defined marks.

3. **Plan Without Schema Marks** - The plan generation (`node_resource_abstract_instance.plan()`) compares values using incomplete marks:
   - Prior state: Has only variable-reference marks (from `priorPaths`)
   - Planned state: Has no marks at all (from provider)
   - Mark comparison triggers false "Update" action even though values are identical

4. **Evaluator Compensation Mismatch** - The `GetResource()` method in `evaluate.go` applies schema marks, but only for expression evaluation—not for planning, creating an asymmetry.

5. **JSON Output Inaccuracy** - The `sensitive_values` in plan JSON output reflects incomplete marks, omitting schema-defined sensitive paths.

The report provides:
- ✅ Detailed evidence with specific file paths and line numbers
- ✅ Code snippets showing the critical flows
- ✅ List of affected components across 4+ packages
- ✅ Ordered causal chain from symptom to root cause
- ✅ Diagnostic steps and fix strategy recommendations

ret, diags\n723: }\n724: \n725: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) plan(\n726: \tctx EvalContext,\n727: \tplannedChange *plans.ResourceInstanceChange,\n728: \tcurrentState *states.ResourceInstanceObject,\n729: \tcreateBeforeDestroy bool,\n730: \tforceReplace []addrs.AbsResourceInstance,\n731: ) (*plans.ResourceInstanceChange, *states.ResourceInstanceObject, planned\n1203: \t// value before comparison. If a\n1206: \t// new mark was also discarded from that config change, it needs to be\n1207: \t// ignored here to prevent an errant update action.\n1208: \tif action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {\n1209: \t\taction = plans.Update\n1210: \t}\n1211: \n1212: \t// As a special case, if we have a previous diff (presumably from the plan\n1213: \t// phases, whereas we're now in the apply phase) and it was for a replace,\n1214: \t// we've already deleted the original object from state by the time we\n1215: \t// get here and so we would've ended up with a _create_ action this time,\n1216: \t// which we now need to paper over to get a result consistent with what\n1217: \t// we originally intended.\n1218: \tif plannedChange != nil {\n1219: \t\tprevChange := *plannedChange\n1220: \t\tif prevChange.Action.IsReplace() && action == plans.Create {\n1221: \t\t\tlog.Printf(\"[TRACE] plan: %s treating Create change as %s change to match with earlier plan\", n.Addr, prevChange.Action)\n1222: \t\t\taction = prevChange.Action\n1223: \t\t\tpriorVal = prevChange.Before\n1224: \t\t}\n1225: \t}\n1226: \n1227: \t// Call post-refresh hook\n1228: \tdiags = diags.Append(ctx.Hook(func(h Hook) (HookAction, error) {\n1229: \t\treturn h.PostDiff(n.Addr, addrs.NotDeposed, action, priorVal, plannedNewVal)\n1230: \t}))\n1231: \tif diags.HasErrors() {\n1232: \t\treturn nil, nil, keyData, diags\n1233: \t}\n1234: \n1235: \t// Update our return plan\n1236: \tplan := &plans.ResourceInstanceChange{\n1237: \t\tAddr:         n.Addr,\n1238: \t\tPrevRunAddr:  n.prevRunAddr(ctx),\n1239: \t\tPrivate:      plannedPrivate,\n1240: \t\tProviderAddr: n.ResolvedProvider,\n1241: \t\tChange: plans.Change{\n1242: \t\t\tAction: reqRep,\n1252: \t}\n1253: \n1254: \t// Update our return state\n1255: \tstate := &states.ResourceInstanceObject{\n1256: \t\t// We use the special \"planned\" status here to note that this\n1257: \t\t// object's value is not yet complete. Objects with this status\n1258: \t\t// cannot be used during expression evaluation, so the caller\n1259: \t\t// must _also_ record the returned change in the active plan,\n1260: \t\t// which the expression evaluator will use in preference to this\n1261: \t\t// incomplete value recorded in the state.\n1262: \t\tStatus:  states.ObjectPlanned,\n1263: \t\tValue:   plannedNewVal,\n1264: \t\tPrivate: plannedPrivate,\n1265: \t}\n1266: \n1267: \treturn plan, state, keyData, diags\n1268: }\n1269: \n1270: func (n *NodeAbstractResource) processIgnoreChanges(prior, config cty.Value, schema *configschema.Block) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1271: \t// ignore_changes only applies when an object already exists, since we\n1272: \t// can't ignore changes to a thing we've not created yet.\n1273: \tif prior.IsNull() {\n1274: \t\treturn config, nil\n1275: \t}\n1276: \n1277: \tignoreChanges := traversalsToPaths(n.Config.Managed.IgnoreChanges)\n1278: \tignoreAll := n.Config.Managed.IgnoreAllChanges\n1279: \n1280: \tif len(ignoreChanges) == 0 && !ignoreAll {\n1281: \t\treturn config, nil\n1282: \t}\n1283: \n1284: \tif ignoreAll {\n1285: \t\t// Legacy providers need up to clean up their invalid plans and ensure\n1286: \t\t// no changes are passed though, but that also means making an invalid\n1287: \t\t// config with computed values. In that case we just don't supply a\n1288: \t\t// schema and return the prior val directly.\n1289: \t\tif schema == nil {\n1290: \t\t\treturn prior, nil\n1291: \t\t}\n1292: \n1293: \t\t// If we are trying to ignore all attribute changes, we must filter\n1294: \t\t// computed attributes out from the prior state to avoid sending them\n1295: \t\t// to the provider as if they were included in the configuration.\n1296: \t\tret, _ := cty.Transform(prior, func(path cty.Path, v cty.Value) (cty.Value, error) {\n1297: \t\t\tattr := schema.AttributeByPath(path)\n1298: \t\t\tif attr != nil && attr.Computed && !attr.Optional {\n1299: \t\t\t\treturn cty.NullVal(v.Type()), nil\n1300: \t\t\t}\n1301: \n1302: \t\t\treturn v, nil\n1303: \t\t})\n1304: \n1305: \t\treturn ret, nil\n1306: \t}\n1307: \n1308: \tif prior.IsNull() || config.IsNull() {\n1309: \t\t// Ignore changes doesn't apply when we're creating for the first time.\n1310: \t\t// Proposed should never be null here, but if it is then we'll just let it be.\n1311: \t\treturn config, nil\n1312: \t}\n1313: \n1314: \tret, diags := processIgnoreChangesIndividual(prior, config, ignoreChanges)\n1315: \n1316: \treturn ret, diags\n1317: }\n1318: \n1319: // Convert the hcl.Traversal values we get form the configuration to the\n1320: // cty.Path values we need to operate on the cty.Values\n1321: func traversalsToPaths(traversals []hcl.Traversal) []cty.Path {\n1322: \tpaths := make([]cty.Path, len(traversals))\n1323: \tfor i, traversal := range traversals {\n1324: \t\tpath := traversalToPath(traversal)\n1325: \t\tpaths[i] = path\n1326: \t}\n1327: \treturn paths\n1328: }\n1329: \n1330: func traversalToPath(traversal hcl.Traversal) cty.Path {\n1331: \tpath := make(cty.Path, len(traversal))\n1332: \tfor si, step := range traversal {\n1333: \t\tswitch ts := step.(type) {\n1334: \t\tcase hcl.TraverseRoot:\n1335: \t\t\tpath[si] = cty.GetAttrStep{\n1336: \t\t\t\tName: ts.Name,\n1337: \t\t\t}\n1338: \t\tcase hcl.TraverseAttr:\n1339: \t\t\tpath[si] = cty.GetAttrStep{\n1340: \t\t\t\tName: ts.Name,\n1341: \t\t\t}\n1342: \t\tcase hcl.TraverseIndex:\n1343: \t\t\tpath[si] = cty.IndexStep{\n1344: \t\t\t\tKey: ts.Key,\n1345: \t\t\t}\n1346: \t\tdefault:\n1347: \t\t\tpanic(fmt.Sprintf(\"unsupported traversal step %#v\", step))\n1348: \t\t}\n1349: \t}\n1350: \treturn path\n1351: }\n1352: \n1353: func processIgnoreChangesIndividual(prior, config cty.Value, ignoreChangesPath []cty.Path) (cty.Value, tfdiags.Diagnostics) {\n1354: \ttype ignoreChange struct {\n1355: \t\t// Path is the full path, minus any trailing map index\n1356: \t\tpath cty.Path\n1357: \t\t// Value is the value we are to retain at the above path. If there is a\n1358: \t\t// key value, this must be a map and the desired value will be at the\n1359: \t\t// key index.\n1360: \t\tvalue cty.Value\n1361: \t\t// Key is the index key if the ignored path ends in a map index.\n1362: \t\tkey cty.Value\n1363: \t}\n1364: \tvar ignoredValues []ignoreChange\n1365: \n1366: \t// Find the actual changes first and store them in the ignoreChange struct.\n1367: \t// If the change was to a map value, and the key doesn't exist in the\n1368: \t// config, it would never be visited in the transform walk.\n1369: \tfor _, icPath := range ignoreChangesPath {\n1370: \t\tkey := cty.NullVal(cty.String)\n1371: \t\t// check for a map index, since maps are the only structure where we\n1372: \t\t// could have invalid path steps.\n1373: \t\tlast, ok := icPath[len(icPath)-1].(cty.IndexStep)\n1374: \t\tif ok {\n1375: \t\t\tif last.Key.Type() == cty.String {\n1376: \t\t\t\ticPath = icPath[:len(icPath)-1]\n1377: \t\t\t\tkey = last.Key\n1378: \t\t\t}\n1379: \t\t}\n1380: \n1381: \t\t// The structure should have been validated already, and we already\n1382: \t\t// trimmed the trailing map index. Any other intermediate index error\n1383: \t\t// means we wouldn't be able to apply the value below, so no need to\n1384: \t\t// record this.\n1385: \t\tp, err := icPath.Apply(prior)\n1386: \t\tif err != nil {\n1387: \t\t\tcontinue\n1388: \t\t}\n1389: \t\tc, err := icPath.Apply(config)\n1390: \t\tif err != nil {\n1391: \t\t\tcontinue\n1392: \t\t}\n1393: \n1394: \t\t// If this is a map, it is checking the entire map value for equality\n1395: \t\t// rather than the individual key. This means that the change is stored\n1396: \t\t// here even if our ignored key doesn't change. That is OK since it\n1397: \t\t// won't cause any changes in the transformation, but allows us to skip\n1398: \t\t// breaking up the maps and checking for key existence here too.\n1399: \t\tif !p.RawEquals(c) {\n1400: \t\t\t// there a change to ignore at this path, store the prior value\n1401: \t\t\tignoredValues = append(ignoredValues, ignoreChange{icPath, p, key})\n1402: \t\t}\n1403: \t}\n1404: \n1405: \tif len(ignoredValues) == 0 {\n1406: \t\treturn config, nil\n1407: \t}\n1408: \n1409: \tret, _ := cty.Transform(config, func(path cty.Path, v cty.Value) (cty.Value, error) {\n1410: \t\t// Easy path for when we are only matching the entire value. The only\n1411: \t\t// values we break up for inspection are maps.\n1412: \t\tif !v.Type().IsMapType() {\n1413: \t\t\tfor _, ignored := range ignoredValues {\n1414: \t\t\t\tif path.Equals(ignored.path) {\n1415: \t\t\t\t\treturn ignored.value, nil\n1416: \t\t\t\t}\n1417: \t\t\t}\n1418: \t\t\treturn v, nil\n1419: \t\t}\n1420: \t\t// We now know this must be a map, so we need to accumulate the values\n1421: \t\t// key-by-key.\n1422: \n1423: \t\tif !v.IsNull() && !v.IsKnown() {\n1424: \t\t\t// since v is not known, we cannot ignore individual keys\n1425: \t\t\treturn v, \n1432: \t\t// The configMap is the current configuration value, which we will\n1433: \t\t// mutate based on the ignored paths and the prior map value.\n1434: \t\tvar configMap map[string]cty.Value\n1435: \t\tswitch {\n1436: \t\tcase v.IsNull() || v.LengthInt() == 0:\n1437: \t\t\tconfigMap = map[string]cty.Value{}\n1438: \t\tdefault:\n1439: \t\t\tconfigMap = v.AsValueMap()\n1440: \t\t}\n1441: \n1442: \t\tfor _, ignored := range ignoredValues {\n1443: \t\t\tif !path.Equals(ignored.path) {\n1444: \t\t\t\tcontinue\n1445: \t\t\t}\n1446: \n1447: \t\t\tif ignored.key.IsNull() {\n1448: \t\t\t\t// The map address is confirmed to match at this point,\n1449: \t\t\t\t// so if there is no key, we want the entire map and can\n1450: \t\t\t\t// stop accumulating values.\n1451: \t\t\t\treturn ignored.value, nil\n1452: \t\t\t}\n1453: \t\t\t// Now we know we are ignoring a specific index of this map, so get\n1454: \t\t\t// the config map and modify, add, or remove the desired key.\n1455: \n1456: \t\t\t// We also need to create a prior map, so we can check for\n1457: \t\t\t// existence while getting the value, because Value.Index will\n1458: \t\t\t// return null for a key with a null value and for a non-existent\n1459: \t\t\t// key.\n1460: \t\t\tvar priorMap map[string]cty.Value\n1461: \n1462: \t\t\t// We need to drop the marks from the \n1467: \t\t\tswitch {\n1468: \t\t\tcase ignored.value.IsNull() || ignoredVal.LengthInt() == 0:\n1469: \t\t\t\tpriorMap = map[string]cty.Value{}\n1470: \t\t\tdefault:\n1471: \t\t\t\tpriorMap = \t\t\tdefault:\n1483: \t\t\t\tconfigMap[key] = priorElem\n1484: \t\t\t}\n1485: \t\t}\n1486: \n1487: \t\tvar newVal cty.Value\n1488: \t\tswitch {\n1489: \t\tcase len(configMap) > 0:\n1490: \t\t\tnewVal \t\t}\n1502: \n1503: \t\treturn newVal, nil\n1504: \t})\n1505: \treturn ret, nil\n1506: }\n1507: \n1508: // readDataSource handles everything needed to call ReadDataSource on the provider.\n1509: // A is\n1677: // returned. If we needed to read a new\n1679: // value, but it still matches the previous state, then we can record a NoNop\n1680: // change. (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) evalApplyProvisioners(ctx EvalContext, state *states.ResourceInstanceObject, createNew bool, when configs.ProvisionerWhen) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n2059: \tvar diags resource.\n2128: func (n *NodeAbstractResourceInstance) applyProvisioners(ctx EvalContext, state *states.ResourceInstanceObject, when configs.ProvisionerWhen, provs []*configs.Provisioner) tfdiags.Diagnostics {\n2129: \tvar diags tfdiags.Diagnostics\n2130: \n2131: \t// this self is only used for destroy provisioner evaluation, and must\n2132: \t// refer to the last known value of the   "content": "# Investigation Report: Phantom In-Place Updates for Resources with Sensitive Attributes\n\n## Summary\n\nTerraform generates phantom in-place updates for resources with provider-schema-defined sensitive attributes because the refresh/plan cycle creates an asymmetry in sensitivity mark application. The provider schema's `Sensitive: true` attribute declarations are never persisted to state, causing the evaluator's compensating mark-application logic to create inconsistencies that trigger false \"Update\" actions when no values have actually changed.\n\n---\n\n## Root Cause\n\nThe root cause is a **sensitivity mark gap** between three critical stages:\n\n1. **State Serialization** (`internal/states/instance_object.go`): When state is written to disk, only sensitivity marks from variable references are saved in `AttrSensitivePaths`; schema-defined sensitive attributes are lost.\n\n2. **State Deserialization** (`internal/states/instance_object_src.go`): When state is read, marks are re-applied from the incomplete `AttrSensitivePaths`, lacking schema marks.\n\n3. **Evaluation-Time Compensation** (`internal/terraform/evaluate.go`): The `GetResource()` method applies schema marks when reading from state for expression evaluation, but this compensating layer is NOT applied during plan generation in `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`.\n\nThis asymmetry causes the plan phase to compare:\n- **Planned state** (from provider, no marks at all)\n- **Prior state** (from state file with incomplete marks, only from variables)\n\nWhen the marks differ even though values don't, a phantom \"Update\" action is triggered.\n\n---\n\n## Evidence\n\n### 1. Sensitivity Marks Lost During State Encoding\n\n**File:** `internal/states/instance_object.go`, lines 94-136\n\n```go\nfunc (o *ResourceInstanceObject) Encode(ty cty.Type, schemaVersion uint64) (*ResourceInstanceObjectSrc, error) {\n    // Extract marks from value before serialization\n    val, pvm := o.Value.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()  // Line 98\n\n    // Convert to JSON (loses all mark information)\n    src, err := ctyjson.Marshal(val, ty)       // Line 111\n\n    // Return object with incomplete marks\n    return &ResourceInstanceObjectSrc{\n        SchemaVersion:      schemaVersion,\n        AttrsJSON:          src,                // JSON has NO marks\n        AttrSensitivePaths: pvm,                // Only marks from variables\n        Private:            o.Private,\n        ...\n    }, nil\n}\n```\n\n**Critical Issue:** `pvm` (path-value marks) extracted at line 98 contains ONLY marks that were already on the value\u2014which come from sensitive variable references, NOT from the provider schema's `Sensitive: true` declarations. The provider schema marks were never on the value in the first place because they're only applied during expression evaluation, not during state persistence.\n\n### 2. Incomplete Marks Re-Applied During State Decoding\n\n**File:** `internal/states/instance_object_src.go`, lines 77-104\n\n```go\nfunc (os *ResourceInstanceObjectSrc) Decode(ty cty.Type) (*ResourceInstanceObject, error) {\n    var val cty.Value\n    ...\n    val, err = ctyjson.Unmarshal(os.AttrsJSON, ty)\n\n    // Re-apply marks from state (INCOMPLETE - missing schema marks)\n    if os.AttrSensitivePaths != nil {\n        val = val.MarkWithPaths(os.AttrSensitivePaths)  // Line 90\n    }\n    ...\n}\n```\n\nThe value is re-marked with `AttrSensitivePaths`, but these paths are incomplete\u2014they lack any paths from the provider schema's `Sensitive: true`.\n\n### 3. Plan Comparison Without Schema Marks\n\n**File:** `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`, lines 725-1250\n\nThe `plan()` method (called from `managedResourceExecute` at line 250 of `node_resource_plan_instance.go`) handles the plan phase:\n\n```go\n// Line 869: Extract marks from prior state (incomplete)\nunmarkedPriorVal, priorPaths := priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n\n// Line 871: Create proposed value\nproposedNewVal := objchange.ProposedNew(schema, unmarkedPriorVal, unmarkedConfigVal)\n\n// Line 902: Call provider (unmarked values sent)\nresp = provider.PlanResourceChange(providers.PlanResourceChangeRequest{\n    TypeName:         n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n    Config:           unmarkedConfigVal,\n    PriorState:       unmarkedPriorVal,        // No schema marks\n    ProposedNewState: proposedNewVal,          // No schema marks\n    ...\n})\n\n// Line 916: Provider response (no marks)\nplannedNewVal := resp.PlannedState\n\n// Line 1082: Compare unmarked values\neqV := unmarkedPlannedNewVal.Equals(unmarkedPriorVal)\neq := eqV.IsKnown() && eqV.True()\n\n// Line 1208: PHANTOM UPDATE TRIGGER\n// If values are equal but marks differ, mark as Update\nif action == plans.NoOp && !marksEqual(filterMarks(plannedNewVal, unmarkedPaths), priorPaths) {\n    action = plans.Update\n}\n```\n\n**Critical Flow:**\n- `priorPaths` contains marks extracted from the state value (line 869)\n- These marks only include marks from sensitive variable references\n- Schema-defined sensitive attributes are NOT in `priorPaths`\n- `plannedNewVal` comes from provider with NO marks\n- Mark comparison at line 1208 can trigger false positives if schema marks should be present\n\n### 4. Refresh Path Reapplies Incomplete Marks\n\n**File:** `internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`, lines 619-723\n\nThe refresh method (called during plan at line 208 of `node_resource_plan_instance.go`):\n\n```go\n// Line 620-626: Extract marks before provider call\npriorVal := state.Value\nvar priorPaths []cty.PathValueMarks\nif priorVal.ContainsMarked() {\n    priorVal, priorPaths = priorVal.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()\n}\n\n// Line 636-641: Provider call (unmarked)\nresp = provider.ReadResource(providers.ReadResourceRequest{\n    TypeName:     n.Addr.Resource.Resource.Type,\n    PriorState:   priorVal,      // Unmarked\n    Private:      state.Private,\n    ProviderMeta: metaConfigVal,\n})\n\n// Line 693: New state from provider\nret.Value = newState\n\n// Line 718-720: Reapply original marks (INCOMPLETE)\nif len(priorPaths) > 0 {\n    ret.Value = ret.Value.MarkWithPaths(priorPaths)\n}\n```\n\n**Issue:** The marks reapplied at line 719 are incomplete because `priorPaths` lacks schema marks.\n\n### 5. Evaluator's Compensating Mark Application\n\n**File:** `internal/terraform/evaluate.go`, lines 541-725\n\nThe `GetResource()` method applies schema marks when reading from state for expression evaluation:\n\n```go\n// Line 718-723: For regular state objects\nif schema.ContainsSensitive() {\n    var marks []cty.PathValueMarks\n    val, marks = val.UnmarkDeepWithPaths()           // Remove existing marks\n    marks = append(marks, schema.ValueMarks(val, nil)...)  // Add schema marks\n    val = val.MarkWithPaths(marks)\n}\n```\n\n**Critical Asymmetry:** This compensating mark application happens ONLY during expression evaluation via `GetResource()`, NOT during:\n- State decoding for planning\n- Provider calls during refresh/plan\n- Difference calculation\n\nThis creates an asymmetry where:\n- Values read FROM state for evaluation have schema marks (via `GetResource()`)\n- Values read FROM state during planning don't have schema marks\n- Planned values from provider have no marks at all\n\n### 6. JSON Output Manifestation\n\n**File:** `internal/command/jsonplan/resource.go`, line 44\n\nThe `SensitiveValues` field in JSON plan output reflects only the marks saved in state:\n\n```go\nSensitiveValues json.RawMessage `json:\"sensitive_values,omitempty\"`\n```\n\nThese are derived from state's `AttrSensitivePaths` (via the plan's change tracking), which lacks schema-defined sensitive paths. This produces incorrect `sensitive_values` in `terraform show -json` output.\n\n---\n\n## Affected Components\n\n1. **`internal/states/instance_object.go`** - Encodes state, loses schema marks\n2. **`internal/states/instance_object_src.go`** - Decodes state, applies incomplete marks\n3. **`internal/terraform/node_resource_abstract_instance.go`** - Plan generation without schema marks\n   - `plan()` method (line 725+)\n   - `refresh()` method (line 580+)\n   - Mark comparison at line 1208\n4. **`internal/terraform/evaluate.go`** - Compensating schema mark application only during evaluation\n   - `GetResource()` method (line 541+)\n5. **`internal/command/jsonplan/`** - JSON output reflects incomplete sensitivity information\n6. **`internal/marks.go`** - Mark equality comparison (`marksEqual()`, `filterMarks()`)\n\n---\n\n## Causal Chain\n\n1. **Provider Response Boundary:** Provider returns `ReadResource` / `PlanResourceChange` response with **no sensitivity marks** (providers don't mark values; Terraform does).\n\n2. **State Persistence Gap:** When state is encoded via `instance_object.Encode()`, only marks that are already on the value are persisted. Schema-defined sensitive marks were never on the value because they're only applied during expression evaluation, so they're lost forever.\n\n3. **Incomplete State Reading:** When state is decoded via `instance_object_src.Decode()`, the re-marked value only has marks from sensitive variable references (stored in `AttrSensitivePaths`), not from schema.\n\n4. **Plan Without Compensation:** During planning in `node_resource_abstract_instance.plan()`, the code:\n   - The planned value has no marks\n   - The prior value has only variable-reference marks\n   - Schema marks are absent from both, but the comparison logic doesn't know they should be there\n\n7. **JSON Output Inaccuracy:** When the plan is serialized to JSON or state, `sensitive_values` reflects only variable-reference sensitivity, omitting schema-defined sensitive attributes.\n\n---\n\n## Diagnostic Evidence\n\n**When phantom updates occur:**\n- `terraform plan` immediately after `terraform apply` shows \"will be updated in-place\"\n- `terraform show -json` shows incomplete `sensitive_values` lacking schema-marked attributes\n- `terraform plan -refresh-only` also shows phantom changes\n- The phantom diff disappears if no provider-schema attributes are marked `Sensitive: true`\n\n**Root Cause Signature:**\n- State file's `sensitive_attributes` lists only paths from variable references\n- Missing paths for all schema-defined `Sensitive: true` attributes\n- Plan comparison detects mark differences even though underlying values are identical\n\n---\n\n## Recommendation\n\n### Fix Strategy\n\nThe core fix requires synchronizing the three stages to use the same mark-application logic:\n\n1. **Apply Schema Marks During State Deserialization** - NOT just during expression evaluation:\n   - In `instance_object_src.Decode()`, after unmarking and remarking with `AttrSensitivePaths`, apply schema marks unconditionally\n   - This ensures that state values always carry complete mark information\n\n2. **Persist Complete Marks to State** - Include schema marks in serialization:\n   - Before encoding state in `instance_object.Encode()`, compute and include schema marks in addition to variable-reference marks\n   - This requires passing the schema to the encode operation (currently it doesn't have access)\n\n3. **Alternative: Skip Mark Comparison for NoOp Actions**:\n   - Remove or modify the check at line 1208 that triggers updates based on mark differences alone\n   - Only treat as Update if actual value changes, not mark-only differences (already done for UnmarkDeep at line 1049-1052)\n\n### Diagnostic Steps\n\n1. Check state file's `sensitive_attributes` section:\n   - Should include paths for ALL schema-defined `Sensitive: true` attributes\n   - Not just those from variable references\n\n2. Compare before/after sensitivity in plan:\n   - `terraform plan -json` should show schema-defined attributes in `sensitive_values`\n\n3. Verify evaluator marks match persistence:\n   - Schema marks applied in `GetResource()` should match marks in state\n\n---\n\n## Impact Assessment\n\nThis issue affects:\n- Any provider with schema attributes marked `Sensitive: true`\n- User confidence in plan accuracy (false positives)\n- State file accuracy (incomplete sensitivity information)\n- JSON output completeness (missing sensitivity metadata)\n\nThe fix would require careful coordination between:\n- State serialization/deserialization layer\n- Plan generation layer\n- Provider schema application layer\n- Expression evaluation layer\n",

1. WRITE /logs/agent/investigation.md
# Investigation Report: Phantom In-Place Updates for Resources with Sensitive Attributes

## Summary

Terraform generates phantom in-place updates for resources with provider-schema-defined sensitive attributes because the refresh/plan cycle creates an asymmetry in sensitivity mark application. The provider schema's `Sensitive: true` attribute declarations are never persisted to state, causing the evaluator's compensating mark-application logic to create inconsistencies that trigger false "Update" actions when no values have actually changed.

---

## Root Cause

The root cause is a **sensitivity mark gap** between three critical stages:

1. **State Serialization** (`internal/states/instance_object.go`): When state is written to disk, only sensitivity marks from variable references are saved in `AttrSensitivePaths`; schema-defined sensitive attributes are lost.

2. **State Deserialization** (`internal/states/instance_object_src.go`): When state is read, marks are re-applied from the incomplete `AttrSensitivePaths`, lacking schema marks.

3. **Evaluation-Time Compensation** (`internal/terraform/evaluate.go`): The `GetResource()` method applies schema marks when reading from state for expression evaluation, but this compensating layer is NOT applied during plan generation in `node_resource_abstract_instance.go`.

This asymmetry causes the plan phase to compare:
- **Planned state** (from provider, no marks at all)
- **Prior state** (from state file with incomplete marks, only from variables)

When the marks differ even though values don't, a phantom "Update" action is triggered.

---

## Evidence

### 1. Sensitivity Marks Lost During State Encoding

**File:** `internal/states/instance_object.go`, lines 94-136

```go
func (o *ResourceInstanceObject) Encode(ty cty.Type, sche
... (truncated)
